
## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Investigation: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/prometheus--ba14bc4 (mirror of prometheus/prometheus)
**Task Type:** Cross-Service Debug (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After a Prometheus upgrade, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The issue correlates with target discovery changes — when targets are added or removed, some remote-write shards stall.

Prometheus logs show:
```
level=info msg="Resharding queues" from=4 to=6
level=info msg="Resharding done" numShards=6
```

But after resharding, metrics show some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. How remote-write queue resharding works (which files/functions)
2. What changed in the resharding logic recently
3. The specific mechanism causing shards to stall
4. Why the issue is intermittent (timing/race condition)
5. Which metrics or logs would confirm the root cause

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `storage/remote/` package, particularly queue management and shard calculation

59-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the Prometheus remote-write queue resharding issue. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**Root Cause:** A **race condition in the metrics counter management** during queue resharding. When new shards are started, the `pendingSamples` counter is immediately reset to 0 (via `Set(0)` at line 1241), but old shards are still running in background goroutines and decrementing this same counter. This creates a critical race condition.

**The Mechanism:**
1. Old shards begin shutting down via `stop()` which closes the `softShutdown` channel
2. Concurrently, `start()` is called which resets `pendingSamples` to 0 while new queues are created
3. If old shards hard-shutdown (exceed `flushDeadline`), they drop remaining samples and decrement the already-reset counter
4. New samples enqueued to new shards increment the counter, but the metric becomes unreliable

**Why It's Intermittent:**
- Only manifests when target discovery changes trigger resharding during active ingestion
- More likely with high sample rates, slow remote endpoints, or frequent resharding
- Timing-dependent on old shard flush duration relative to `flushDeadline`

**Evidence Points:**
- Lines 1237-1266: `start()` method resets counter too early
- Lines 1184-1199: `reshardLoop()` doesn't synchronize counter state
- Lines 1071-1074: `numShards` updated before actual resharding completes
- Lines 1563-1578: Old `runShard()` goroutines may decrement counter after hard shutdown

The report I created includes:
- Detailed code references with line numbers
- Specific race condition scenarios  
- Why the issue is intermittent and load-dependent
- Diagnostic steps to confirm the root cause in production
- Recommended fix strategies

Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := func(try int) error {\n591: \t\tctx, span := otel.Tracer(\"\").Start(ctx, \"Remote Metadata Send Batch\")\n592: \t\tdefer span.End()\n593: \n594: \t\tspan.SetAttributes(\n595: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"metadata\", metadataCount),\n596: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"try\", try),\n597: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_name\", t.storeClient.Name()),\n598: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_url\", t.storeClient.Endpoint()),\n599: \t\t)\n600: \t\t// Attributes defined by OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n601: \t\tif try > 0 {\n602: \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n603: \t\t}\n604: \n605: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n606: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since it's\n607: \t\t// embedded in v2 calls now, and we do v1 here.\n608: \t\t_, err := t.storeClient.Store(ctx, req, try)\n609: \t\tt.metrics.sentBatchDuration.Observe(time.Since(begin).Seconds())\n610: \n611: \t\tif err != nil {\n612: \t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n613: \t\t\treturn err\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\treturn nil\n616: \t}\n617: \n618: \tretry := func() {\n619: \t\tt.metrics.retriedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n620: \t}\n621: \terr = t.sendWriteRequestWithBackoff(ctx, attemptStore, retry)\n622: \tif err != nil {\n623: \t\treturn err\n624: \t}\n625: \tt.metrics.metadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n626: \tt.metrics.metadataBytesTotal.Add(float64(len(req)))\n627: \treturn nil\n628: }\n629: \n630: func isSampleOld(baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration, ts int64) bool {\n631: \tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n632: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n633: \t\treturn false\n634: \t}\n635: \tlimitTs := baseTime.Add(-sampleAgeLimit)\n636: \tsampleTs := timestamp.Time(ts)\n637: \treturn sampleTs.Before(limitTs)\n638: }\n639: \n640: func isTimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n641: \treturn func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n642: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n643: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n644: \t\t\treturn false\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tswitch {\n647: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n648: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n649: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n650: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n651: \t\t\t\treturn true\n652: \t\t\t}\n653: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n654: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, \t\t\t}\n663: \t\tdefault:\n664: \t\t\treturn false\n665: \t\t}\n666: \t\treturn false\n667: \t}\n668: }\n669: \n670: func isV2TimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n671: \treturn func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n672: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n673: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we Blocks until all samples are\n701: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n702: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n703: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n704: outer:\n705: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n706: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n707: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n711: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n712: \t\tif !ok {\n713: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n714: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n715: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n716: \t\t\t} else {\n717: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n718: \t\t\t}\n719: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n720: \t\t\tcontinue\n721: \t\t}\n722: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n723: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n724: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n725: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n726: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. This should not be t.cfg.MinBackoff\n727: \t\t// as it can happen without errors, and we want to pickup work after\n728: \t\t// filling a queue/resharding as quickly as possible.\n729: \t\t// TODO: Consider using the average duration of a request as the backoff.\n730: \t\tbackoff := model.Duration(5 * time.Millisecond)\n731: \t\tfor {\n732: \t\t\tselect {\n733: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n734: \t\t\t\treturn false\n735: \t\t\tdefault:\n736: \t\t\t}\n737: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{\n738: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n739: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n740: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:    s.T,\n741: \t\t\t\tvalue:        s.V,\n742: \t\t\t\tsType:        tSample,\n743: \t\t\t}) {\n744: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n745: \t\t\t}\n746: \n747: \t\t\tt.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n748: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n749: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n750: \t\t\t// It is reasonable to use t.cfg.MaxBackoff here, as if we have hit\n751: \t\t\t// the full backoff we are likely waiting for external resources.\n752: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n753: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n754: \t\t\t}\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t}\n757: \treturn true\n758: }\n759: \n760: func (t *QueueManager) AppendExemplars(exemplars []record.RefExemplar) bool {\n761: \tif !t.sendExemplars {\n762: \t\treturn true\n763: \t}\n764: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n765: outer:\n766: \tfor _, e := \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n930: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n931: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n932: and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n954: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n955: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n956: \tt.shards.stop()\n957: \tt.watcher.Stop()\n958: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n959: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Stop()\n960: \t}\n961: \tt.metrics.unregister()\n962: }\n963: \n964: // StoreSeries keeps track of which series we know about for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n969: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n970: \tfor _, s := range series {\n971: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert into seriesSegmentIndexes map StoreMetadata(meta []record.RefMetadata) {\n988: \tif t.protoMsg == config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n989: \t\treturn\n990: \t}\n991: \n992: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n993: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n994: \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. Used when only client specific\n1034: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1035: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1036: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1037: \tt.storeClient = c\n1038: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1039: }\n1040: \n1041: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1042: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1043: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1044: \treturn t.storeClient\n1045: }\n1046: \n1047: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. If b contains\n1048: // a label in externalLabels, the value in b wins.\n1049: func processExternalLabels(b *labels.Builder, externalLabels []labels.Label) {\n1050: \tfor _, el := range externalLabels {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1217: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1218: \n1219: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1220: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1221: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown    atomic.Uint32\n1231: \texemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown  atomic.Uint32\n1232: \thistogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown atomic.Uint32\n1233: \tmetadataDroppedOnHardShutdown   atomic.Uint32\n1234: }\n1235: \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = newQueue(s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, s.qm.cfg.Capacity)\n1247: \t}\n1248: \n1249: \ts.queues = newQueues\n1250: \n1251: \tvar hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n1252: \thardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n1265: \t}\n1266: }\n1267: \n1268: // stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.\n1269: func (s *shards) stop() {\n1270: \t// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1329: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()\n1330: \t\t\ts.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()\n1331: \t\tcase tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:\n1332: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()\n1333: \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1334: \t\tdefault:\n1335: \t\t\treturn true\n1336: \t\t}\n1337: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1338: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1361: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1362: \ttimestamp      int64\n1363: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1364: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1365: \tsType seriesType\n1366: }\n1367: \n1368: type seriesType int\n1369: \n1370: const (\n1371: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1372: \ttExemplar\n1373: \ttHistogram\n1374: \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),\n1387: \t\tbatchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),\n1388: \t\t// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for\n1389: \t\t// the batch being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1446: // made after this is called.\n1447: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1448: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1449: \t\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\n1450: \t}\n1451: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1452: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1453: \tq.batch = nil\n1454: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1455: }\n1456: \n1457: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = q.batchPool[:batches-1]\n1486: \t\treturn batch\n1487: \t}\n1488: \treturn make([]timeSeries, 0, capacity)\n1489: }\n1490: \n1491: func (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n1492: \tdefer func() {\n1493: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1494: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \t}()\n1497: \n1498: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1499: \tsymbolTable := \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, WriteResponseStats, duration time.Duration) {\n1662: \t// Partial errors may happen -- account for that.\n1663: \tsampleDiff := sampleCount - rs.Samples\n1664: \tif sampleDiff > 0 {\n1665: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(sampleDiff))\n1666: \t}\n1667: \thistogramDiff := histogramCount - rs.Histograms\n1668: \tif histogramDiff > 0 {\n1669: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedHistogramsTotal.Add(float64(histogramDiff))\n1670: \t}\n1671: \texemplarDiff := exemplarCount - rs.Exemplars\n1672: \tif exemplarDiff > 0 {\n1673: \"failedHistogramCount\", histogramDiff, \"failedExemplarCount\", exemplarDiff, \"err\", err)\n1677: \t} else if sampleDiff+exemplarDiff+histogramDiff > 0 {\n1678: \t\ts.qm.logger.Error(\"we got 2xx status code from the Receiver yet statistics indicate some data was not written; investigation needed\", \"failedSampleCount\", sampleDiff, \"failedHistogramCount\", histogramDiff, \"failedExemplarCount\", exemplarDiff)\n1679: \t}\n1680: \n1681: \t// These counters are used to calculate the dynamic sharding, and as such\n1682: \t// should be maintained irrespective of success or failure.\n1683: \ts.qm.dataOut.incr(int64(sampleCount + exemplarCount + histogramCount + metadataCount))\n1684: \ts.qm.dataOutDuration.incr(int64(duration))\n1685: sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount, metadataCount int, pBuf *proto.Buffer, buf compression.EncodeBuffer, compr compression.Type) (WriteResponseStats, error) {\n1699: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no metadata.\n1700: \treq, highest, lowest, err := buildWriteRequest(s.qm.logger, samples, nil, pBuf, nil, buf, compr)\n1701: \ts.qm.buildRequestLimitTimestamp.Store(lowest)\n1702: \tif err != nil {\n1703: \t\t// Failing to build the write request is non-recoverable, since it will\n1704: \t\t// only error if marshaling the proto to bytes fails.\n1705: \t\treturn WriteResponseStats{}, err\n1706: \t}\n1707: \n1708: \treqSize := len(req)\n1709: \n1710: \t// Since we retry writes via attemptStore and sendWriteRequestWithBackoff we need\n1711: \t// to track the total amount of accepted data across the various attempts.\n1712: \taccumulatedStats := WriteResponseStats{}\n1713: \tvar accumulatedStatsMu sync.Mutex\n1714: \taddStats := func(rs WriteResponseStats) {\n1715: \t\taccumulatedStatsMu.Lock()\n1716: \t\taccumulatedStats = accumulatedStats.Add(rs)\n1717: \t\taccumulatedStatsMu.Unlock()\n1718: \t}\n1719: \n1720: \t// An anonymous function allows us to defer the func(int) error, onRetry func()) error {\n1982: \tbackoff := t.cfg.MinBackoff\n1983: \tsleepDuration := model.Duration(0)\n1984: \ttry := 0\n1985: \n1986: \tfor {\n1987: \t\tselect {\n1988: \t\tcase duration specified by Retry-After header\", \"duration\", sleepDuration)\n2010: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter < 0:\n2011: \t\t\tt.logger.Debug(\"retry-after cannot be in past, retrying using default backoff mechanism\")\n2012: \t\t}\n2013: \n2014: \t\t// We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015: \t\t// make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016: \t\t//\n2017: \t\t// reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018: \t\t// is disabled.   "content": "# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe intermittent stalling of remote-write shards after resharding is caused by a **race condition in the metrics counter reset** combined with **asynchronous queue shutdown timing**. When `start()` is called on new shards, it immediately resets `pendingSamples` to zero, but old shards are still in the background flushing data and decrementing this same counter. Additionally, samples enqueued during the transition window between `stop()` and `start()` may end up in queues that are being hard-shutdown before they can be sent.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1237-1266` (`start()` method) and lines 1184-1199 (`reshardLoop()`)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n\nThe resharding process has a critical flaw in how it manages the pending samples metric during queue transitions:\n\n1. **Premature Counter Reset** (line 1241):\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n       s.mtx.Lock()\n       defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- RESETS COUNTER IMMEDIATELY\n       ...\n   }\n   ```\n   This resets the counter to 0 immediately when new shards start.\n\n2. **Race with Old Shards Cleanup**:\n   ```go\n   func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n       for {\n           select {\n           case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n               t.shards.stop()         // Old shards close softShutdown, start flushing\n               t.shards.start(numShards)  // New shards created, counter reset to 0\n           ...\n           }\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n   Between `stop()` and `start()`:\n   - Old shards close `softShutdown` channel to block new enqueues\n   - Old shards begin `FlushAndShutdown()` on their queues\n   - If flush takes longer than expected, old shards hard-shutdown via context cancellation\n   - **Concurrently**: `start()` resets `pendingSamples` to 0\n   - Old shards' `runShard()` goroutines continue decrementing this counter as they finish sending\n\n3. **Hard Shutdown Timeout Behavior** (line 1286-1294):\n   ```go\n   select {\n   case <-s.done:\n       return\n   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):  // Typically 30 seconds\n   }\n   // Force an unclean shutdown\n   s.hardShutdown()  // Cancels context, old runShard goroutines exit\n   <-s.done\n   ```\n\n   If old shards don't complete flushing within `flushDeadline`:\n   - Context is cancelled via `s.hardShutdown()`\n   - Remaining samples in old queues are dropped\n   - Old `runShard` goroutines decrement `pendingSamples` for these dropped samples\n   - But counter was already reset to 0, so it never recovers\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**File: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**\n\n- **Lines 1071-1074** (`updateShardsLoop`): Updates `t.numShards` immediately after sending reshape request, before actual resharding completes\n  ```go\n  case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n      t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n      t.numShards = desiredShards  // <-- Updated before reshardLoop processes it\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1184-1199** (`reshardLoop`): Asynchronously processes reshard requests\n  ```go\n  func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n      for {\n          select {\n          case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n              t.shards.stop()         // Closes softShutdown, begins flushing\n              t.shards.start(numShards)  // Creates new queues, resets counter\n          ...\n          }\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1237-1266** (`start`): Problematic counter reset\n  ```go\n  func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n      s.mtx.Lock()\n      defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // BUG: Resets while old shards still active\n      ...\n      s.queues = newQueues\n      ...\n      for i := range n {\n          go s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1325-1327** (enqueue): Increments counter when samples enqueued\n  ```go\n  case tSample:\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n      s.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1689-1691** (updateMetrics): Decrements counter when samples sent\n  ```go\n  s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(sampleCount))\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1563-1578** (runShard hard shutdown): Drops samples when context cancelled\n  ```go\n  case <-ctx.Done():\n      droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // <-- Sub after Set(0)\n      ...\n  ```\n\n### Intermittency Explanation\n\nThe issue is intermittent because:\n\n1. **Timing-dependent**: The race condition only manifests when:\n   - Target discovery changes trigger resharding during active sample ingestion\n   - Old shards' flush takes longer than expected (> flushDeadline)\n   - New samples are enqueued during the transition window\n\n2. **Load-dependent**: Occurs more frequently under:\n   - High sample ingestion rates (more samples in flight during transition)\n   - Slow remote storage endpoints (longer flush time for old shards)\n   - Frequent target discovery changes (more resharding events)\n\n3. **Scale-dependent**: More visible at:\n   - Larger shard counts (more goroutines in transition)\n   - Higher capacity configs (more samples buffered in queues)\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**:\n   - `QueueManager` struct (manages resharding)\n   - `shards` struct (represents parallel send queues)\n   - `start()` method (initializes new shards)\n   - `stop()` method (shuts down old shards)\n   - `reshardLoop()` (processes reshard events)\n   - `updateShardsLoop()` (decides when to reshard)\n   - `enqueue()` function (enqueues samples to shards)\n   - `runShard()` goroutine (sends batches, updates metrics)\n\n2. **`storage/remote` package**:\n   - Metrics tracking pending samples\n   - WAL watcher integration that calls `Append()`\n\n## Root Cause Analysis: Why Shards Stall\n\nThe stalling occurs through this sequence:\n\n1. **Reshape triggered**: Target discovery change \u2192 desired shards change (e.g., 4 \u2192 6)\n\n2. **Async reshard starts**:\n   ```\n   updateShardsLoop sends to reshardChan\n   reshardLoop receives: stop() old shards, start() new shards\n   ```\n\n3. **Old shards shutdown**:\n   - `stop()` closes `softShutdown` channel\n   - WAL watcher's `enqueue()` calls fail (return false)\n   - New samples in-flight retry with backoff\n\n4. **Critical race - Counter reset**:\n   - `start()` acquires write lock\n   - Sets `pendingSamples = 0` (line 1241)\n   - Creates new queues and starts new `runShard` goroutines\n   - Releases lock\n\n5. **Samples enqueued to new shards**:\n   - WAL watcher's retries succeed on new shards\n   - Samples are `Append()`ed to new queues\n   - `pendingSamples` is incremented for each sample\n\n6. **Potential stall scenarios**:\n\n   **Scenario A - Partial batch buffering**:\n   - New samples are buffered in queue's partial batch\n   - Batch doesn't fill up to capacity\n   - Batch timeout (10+ seconds) waiting for more samples\n   - If no new samples arrive, `runShard` timer eventually flushes batch\n\n   **Scenario B - Hard shutdown during transition**:\n   - Old shards exceed `flushDeadline` waiting to send\n   - `hardShutdown()` cancels old context\n   - Old `runShard` goroutines exit, dropping queued samples\n   - They call `Sub(droppedSamples)` on counter already reset to 0\n   - Counter tracking becomes inconsistent\n\n   **Scenario C - Queue channel deadlock**:\n   - Sample enqueued during transition window\n   - Ends up in old shard's batch that's never flushed\n   - Or in new shard queue that runShard never reads from\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe `start()` method should NOT reset `pendingSamples` to 0 unconditionally. Instead:\n\n1. **Preserve old shard metrics**: Don't reset the counter; let old shards naturally decrement it as they complete\n2. **Alternative**: Only reset counter AFTER confirming old shards are fully stopped\n3. **Or**: Atomically transfer pending count from old shards to new shards\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this root cause in a live system:\n\n1. **Monitor these metrics during resharding**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` (should not jump to 0)\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` (actual number of shards)\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` (target number)\n\n2. **Enable debug logging** in queue_manager:\n   - Watch for \"Remote storage resharding\" messages\n   - Check timestamps against \"Resharding done\"\n   - Look for \"(Currently resharding, skipping.)\" messages (queue blocked)\n\n3. **Examine for stuck samples**:\n   ```promql\n   # High pending with zero output rate\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending > 0\n   and\n   rate(prometheus_remote_storage_samples_total[1m]) == 0\n\n   # Check for specific shards stuck\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending\n   without (job, instance) by (shard)\n   ```\n\n4. **Look for dropped samples**:\n   - Check if `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` increased during resharding\n   - This would indicate hard shutdown occurred\n\n5. **Check logs for timeout messages**:\n   - Search for flush deadline exceeded during resharding\n   - These correlate with hard shutdown dropping samples\n\n### Prevention Measures\n\n1. **Increase `flushDeadline`** in queue config if resharding frequently fails\n2. **Reduce resharding frequency** by tuning `shardUpdateDuration` (currently 10 seconds)\n3. **Monitor resharding events** and correlation with:\n   - Target discovery changes\n   - Sample ingestion rate spikes\n   - Remote storage latency increases\n\n## Related Code\n\n- CHANGELOG.md mentions issue #7122 \"Fixed blocked resharding edge case\" (line 1457)\n- This investigation suggests the fix may have been incomplete or partially reverted\n- The core issue of counter reset during transition persists\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/investigation.md"

# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

## Summary

The intermittent stalling of remote-write shards after resharding is caused by a **race condition in the metrics counter reset** combined with **asynchronous queue shutdown timing**. When `start()` is called on new shards, it immediately resets `pendingSamples` to zero, but old shards are still in the background flushing data and decrementing this same counter. Additionally, samples enqueued during the transition window between `stop()` and `start()` may end up in queues that are being hard-shutdown before they can be sent.

## Root Cause

**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1237-1266` (`start()` method) and lines 1184-1199 (`reshardLoop()`)

**Mechanism:**

The resharding process has a critical flaw in how it manages the pending samples metric during queue transitions:

1. **Premature Counter Reset** (line 1241):
   ```go
   func (s *shards) start(n int) {
       s.mtx.Lock()
       defer s.mtx.Unlock()
       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- RESETS COUNTER IMMEDIATELY
       ...
   }
   ```
   This resets the counter to 0 immediately when new shards start.

2. **Race with Old Shards Cleanup**:
   ```go
   func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {
       for {
           select {
           case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:
               t.shards.stop()         // Old shards close softShutdown, start flushing
               t.shards.start(numShards)  // New shards created, counter reset to 0
           ...
           }
       }
   }
   ```

   Between `stop()` and `start()`:
   - Old shards close `softShutdown` channel to block new enqueues
   - Old shards begin `FlushAndShutdown()` on their queues
   - If flush takes longer than expected, old shards hard-shutdown via context
... (truncated)
